\title{Characterizations of Bounded Spectral Multipliers on Manifolds with Periodic Geodesic Flow}
\author{Jacob Denson\footnote{University of Madison Wisconsin, Madison, WI, jcdenson@wisc.edu}}

\begin{document}

\maketitle

\begin{abstract}
    It is a well known result of Mitjagin that on a compact Riemannian manifold $M$, and for a function $m: (0,\infty) \to \CC$, if the spectral multiplier operators $m(\sqrt{-\Delta}/R)$ are uniformly bounded on $L^p(M)$ for $R > 0$, then the radial function $m(|\cdot|): \RR^d \to \CC$ induces a bounded Fourier multiplier operator on $L^p(\RR^d)$. In this paper, we prove the converse for manifolds in which the geodesic flow is periodic, of dimension $d \geq 4$ and for $(d-1)^{-1} \leq |1/p - 1/2| \leq 1/2$. In the process, we find an effective characterization of the functions $m$ for which the operators $m(\sqrt{-\Delta}/R)$ are uniformly bounded in $L^p(M)$ for this range of $p$, which can be viewed as a variable-coefficient analogue of the results of Heo, Nasarov and Seeger.

    % In particular, this covers the case where $M = S^d$ is the sphere, in which case the spectral multipliers can be viewed as zonal convolution operators, as well as for other rank one compact symmetric spaces.

    %Let $M$ be a $d$-dimensional compact Riemannian manifold, and $P = \sqrt{-\Delta}$ the square root of the Laplace-Beltrami operator on $M$. A result of Mitjagin states that for a function $h: (0,\infty) \to \mathbb{C}$, if the family of spectral multipliers $\{ h(P/R) : R > 0 \}$ are uniformly bounded on $L^p(M)$, then the radial function $h(|\cdot|): \mathbb{R}^d \to \mathbb{C}$ induces a bounded Fourier multiplier operator on $L^p(\mathbb{R}^d)$. We prove the converse of Mitjagin's result for $d \geq 4$ and $(d-1)^{-1} \leq |1/p - 1/2| \leq 1/2$, under the assumption that the geodesic flow on $M$ is periodic.  %, i.e. whether the $L^p$-boundedness of the Fourier multiplier corresponding to $h(|\cdot|)$ implies that the operators $\{ h(\sqrt{-\Delta}/R) \}$ are uniformly bounded on $L^p(M)$.
%In particular, this result includes the case when $M$ is the $d$-dimensional sphere, where the spectral multipliers can be viewed as zonal convolution operators. In doing so, we find an effective characterization of the functions $h$ for which the associated spectral multiplier operators $\{ h(P/R) \}$ are uniformly bounded on $L^p(M)$ for the same range of $p$ and $d$, which can 

%    We completely characterize the $L^p$ bounded multipliers of the Laplace-Beltrami operator on $S^d$, for $1 < p < 2(d-1)/(d+1)$ and $(d-3)/2(d-1) < p < \infty$. This requires robust variants of the methods of Heo, Nasarov, and Seeger, who characterized $L^p$ bounded radial Fourier multipliers, to variable-coefficient settings. To obtain this characterization, we combine quasi-orthogonality bounds for small-time localized solutions to the half-wave equation on a compact manifold $M$, which we obtain by studying oscillatory integrals emerging from the Lax-H\"{o}rmander parametrix for the half-wave equation, with variants of the geometric density arguments introduced by Heo, Nasarov, and Seeger.
\end{abstract}

\section{Introduction}

Let $M$ be a compact Riemannian manifold of dimension $d$, let $\Delta$ be it's Laplace-Beltrami operator, and let $P = \sqrt{-\Delta}$. For any bounded function $m: (0,\infty) \to \CC$, we can define a spectral multiplier operator $m(P)$. In this paper, we study the relation between the $L^p$ boundedness of the dilated multipliers $m_\rho(P)$ for $\rho > 0$, where $m_\rho(\lambda) = m(\lambda / \rho)$, and the $L^p$ boundedness of the radial Fourier multiplier operator $T_m$ on $\RR^d$ defined by setting
%
\[ T_m f(x) = \int_{\RR^d} m(|\xi|) \widehat{f}(\xi) e^{2 \pi i \xi \cdot x}\; d\xi \quad\quad\text{for $f: \RR^d \to \CC$.} \]
%
In particular, we show that for any $p \in [1,\infty]$, if $d$ is sufficiently large, then the $L^p$ boundedness of $T_m$ is equivalent to the uniform $L^p$ boundedness of the operators $m_\rho(P)$, provided that the geodesic flow on $M$ is periodic.

\begin{theorem} \label{maintheoremprime}
    Suppose $M$ is a compact Riemannian manifold, and the geodesic flow on $M$ is periodic. If $d \geq 4$, and $1/(d-1) \leq |1/p - 1/2| \leq 1/2$, then
    %
    \[ \sup\nolimits_\rho \| m_\rho(P) \| \sim \| T_m \|, \]
    %
    where $\| T_m \|$ is the operator norm on $L^p(\RR^d)$, and $\| m_\rho(P) \|$ the operator norm on $L^p(M)$. The implicit constant depends only on $M$ and $p$
\end{theorem}

One side of this inequality is already known. A classical transplantation theorem of Mitjagin \cite{Mitjagin} states that
%
\begin{equation}
\label{mitjagininequality}
    \| T_m \| \lesssim \sup\nolimits_\rho \| m_\rho(P) \|.
\end{equation}
%
Moreover, this inequality is known to hold for the larger range of exponents $1 \leq p \leq \infty$ and for general compact manifolds $M$ (see \cite{KenigStantonTomas} for an english translation of Mitjagin's proof). The result is intuitive if we consider the geometry in \eqref{mitjagininequality}; if we let $\Delta_\rho$ be the Laplace-Beltrami operator on $M$ associated with the dilated metric $g_\rho = \rho^{-2} g$, and define $P_\rho = \sqrt{-\Delta_\rho}$, then $m_\rho(P) = m(P_\rho)$. As $\rho \to \infty$, the metric $g_\rho$ gives the manifold $M$ less curvature and more volume, and as $\rho \to \infty$ we might therefore expect $M$ equipped with $\Delta_\rho$ to behave more and more like $\RR^d$ equipped with the usual Laplace operator $\Delta_{\RR^d} = \sum \partial_j^2$. Indeed, Mitjagin's proof essentially shows that in coordinates, $m_\rho(P)$ converges to $m(\Delta_{\RR^d})$ as $\rho \to \infty$, in an appropriate sense, and since $m(\Delta_{\RR^d})$ is just the operator $T_m$, \eqref{mitjagininequality} follows.

\begin{comment}
%
\[ \widehat{m}(t) e^{2 \pi i t P/R} dt \]

one can write $m_R(P) = m(P_R)$, where $P_R = \sqrt{-\Delta_R}$ for the Laplace-Beltrami operator $\Delta_R$ of the manifold $M$, equipped with a rescaled metric $g_R = R^{-2} g$, and as $R \to \infty$, this rescaled metric becomes flatter and flatter, and $\text{Vol}(M,g_R) \sim R^d$.
\end{comment}

The novel result in this paper is a proof of the converse inequality to \eqref{mitjagininequality} under the assumption that the geodesic flow on $M$ is periodic, i.e. a proof that
%
\begin{equation} \label{upperboundmainresult}
    \sup\nolimits_\rho \| T_\rho \| \lesssim \| T_m \| \quad\quad \text{if}\quad \frac{1}{d-1} \leq \left| \frac{1}{p} - \frac{1}{2} \right| \leq \frac{1}{2}.
\end{equation}
%
Equation \eqref{upperboundmainresult} is more surprising than equation \eqref{mitjagininequality}, since it is not geometrically intuitive why $L^p$ bounds of a Fourier multiplier on a flat space should imply uniform $L^p$ bounds for a family of spectral mulipliers on a curved space. No variants of \eqref{upperboundmainresult} are currently known for any manifold and any value of $p \neq 2$; the only exception is in the study of multipliers on $\TT^d$, where one has more robust tools, like the Poisson summation formula, to relate $L^p$ bounds for multipliers on $\TT^d$ and $L^p$ bounds for multipliers on $\RR^d$ (see Section 3.6.2 of \cite{Grafakos}). Note also that $\TT^d$ is a Riemannian manifold with no curvature.

% It is still unclear whether one can improve \eqref{upperboundmainresult} to a wider range of $p$ or to a more general family of compact Riemannian manifolds. At least for values of $p$ with $|1/p - 1/2| \leq 1/2d$, a very different approach is likely required than the approach given in this paper, since Equation \eqref{heonazarovestimate}, discussed in the next paragraph, is a key part of the proof of \eqref{upperboundmainresult}, and \eqref{heonazarovestimate} can only possibly be extended to the range $|1/p - 1/2| > 1/2d$. Even then, proving this extension is immensely difficult, implying the Bochner-Riesz conjecture in it's full range, and thus the Restriction and Kakeya conjectures.

The path to proving \eqref{upperboundmainresult} without being able to relate the geometry of the two spaces is hinted at by the main result of \cite{HeoandNazarovandSeeger}, which states that, for $(d-1)^{-1} \leq |1/p - 1/2| \leq 1/2$, $\| T_m \| \sim C_p(m)$, where
%
\[ C_p(m) = \sup_{h > 0} \left( \int_0^\infty \Big[ \langle t \rangle^{\alpha(p)} |\widehat{m}_h(t)| \Big]^p\; dt \right)^{1/p}. \]
%
Here $\alpha(p) = (d-1)|1/p - 1/2|$, and $m_h(\lambda) = m(2^h \lambda) \chi(\lambda)$ for any fixed choice of a smooth, compactly supported function $\chi$ with support on $[1/2,2]$ for which $\sum \chi(2^h \lambda) = 1$. Since $\sup_{\rho > 0} C_p(m_\rho) \sim C_p(m)$, and duality implies that the operator norm of $m(P)$ on $L^p(M)$ is equal to the operator norm of $m(P)$ on $L^{p'}(M)$ for $1/p + 1/p' = 1$, Theorem \ref{maintheoremprime} therefore follows from the following estimate.

\begin{prop} \label{mainTheorem}
    Suppose $1 \leq p \leq 2(d-1)/(d+1)$. Then for any function $m: (0,\infty) \to \CC$,
    %
    \[ \| m(P) \| \lesssim C_p(m), \]
    %
    where the implicit constant depends only on $p$ and the manifold $M$.
\end{prop}

The techniques that underlie the proof of Proposition \ref{mainTheorem} are also inspired by the proof methods of \cite{HeoandNazarovandSeeger}. As in that proof, we begin by considering a decomposition $m(\cdot) = \sum_j m_j(\cdot / 2^j)$, where $\text{supp}(m_j) \subset [1/2,2]$. We will see that the behaviour of the multipliers $m_j(P/2^j)$ is fairly benign for $j \lesssim 1$. Proposition \ref{mainTheorem} then follows if we can show that for each $j \gtrsim 10$,
%
\begin{equation} \label{dyadicMainReulst}
    \| m_j(P/2^j) \| \lesssim \| \langle t \rangle^{s_p} \widehat{m}_j(t) \|_{L^p(\RR)},
\end{equation}
%
and also that
%
\begin{equation} \label{puttingTogetherPieces}
    \Big\| \sum_{j \gtrsim 1} m_j(P/2^j) \Big\| \lesssim \sup_{j \gtrsim 1} \| m_j(P/2^j) \|.
\end{equation}
%
We prove \eqref{dyadicMainReulst} by obtaining some new quasi-orthogonality estimates for averages of solutions to the half-wave equation on $M$, which reduces our analysis to a geometric `density-decomposition' argument involving geodesic annuli on $M$. We then use variants of Littlewood-Paley theory and the theory of atomic decompositions to obtain \eqref{puttingTogetherPieces}.

\begin{comment}
